Cause and Condition in Hajj and the Linguistic Analysis of 'an'
Refined usul rule applied to Hajj, with linguistic analysis of 'an'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of identifying a cause through the word 'an' and distinguish cause from condition in Hajj.

Core Idea
The word 'an' in hadith extracts the cause by eliminating the impossible; the House causes Hajj, but time and ability are conditions.

This lesson focuses on the latter part of the passage, where the author applies the same principle to Hajj and refines the analysis using the preposition 'an'. The cause of Hajj is the House itself, as shown by attribution and absence of repetition. The time of Hajj and financial ability are conditions. The detailed reasoning with 'an' demonstrates Hanafi linguistic usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Hajj is obligated once in a lifetime. The cause must be something attributed to the act and not repeating.
2
Analyze the linguistic attribution
The Quran says 'Hajj of the House' (حج البيت) – the House is attributed to the act, indicating it is the cause.
No repetition: Hajj is not required multiple times from the same person.
3
Check for repetition
Hajj does not multiply with the House; it is a single obligation. Thus, the House is not a cause for multiple obligations; it is the cause for the single obligation.
The author says 'it does not repeat' to show it is not a cause in the sense of multiplication but still a cause because of attribution.
4
Differentiate conditions: time and ability
The time (season) and financial ability are not attributed to the act linguistically (e.g., 'Hajj of the time' is not used) and do not repeat. They are conditions for performance.
5
Refine using the word 'an'
The hadith for zakat uses 'an' to extract the cause. Apply the same method: 'an' indicates extraction, so the object is either cause or locus. For zakat, the dependent heads are causes. For Hajj, there is no such hadith, but the principle is consistent.

وصحَّ الأداء بعده من المسافر، وقد تأخر الخطاب به عنه، ولهذا جب على صبي يبلغ في بعض شهر رمضان، وكافر يُسلم بقدر ما أدركه ؛

Rejecting Hadith Conflicting with Quran: The Hanafi Rule
Establishes rules for hidden discontinuity due to conflict with Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a hadith that contradicts the Quran and apply the Hanafi rule that such a hadith is rejected as having hidden discontinuity, explaining that a khabar wahid cannot specify or abrogate the Quran.

Core Idea
A khabar wahid cannot override the Quran because the Quran is certain and the hadith is speculative.

This passage introduces a key principle in Hanafi usul: a hadith that contradicts the Quran is considered to have hidden discontinuity (inqita' batin) and is therefore rejected. The reasoning is that the Quran is established with certainty (qat'i), while a khabar wahid (isolated report) is speculative (zanni). Consequently, the general (amm) of the Quran cannot be specified (takhsis) by a khabar wahid, nor can the Quran be abrogated or added to by such reports. This principle distinguishes the Hanafi school from the Shafi'i school, which allows specification.

Guided Path
1
Understand hidden discontinuity (inqita' batin)
Hidden discontinuity is not apparent from the chain of transmission but is discovered by testing the hadith against established principles (usul). One type is contradiction (mu'arada) with a definitive source.
This is a memorization anchor: inqita' batin is detected by content, not chain.
2
Identify the four criteria for contradiction
The passage lists four criteria that trigger rejection: (1) contradicts the Quran, (2) contradicts known sunnah, (3) is shadhdh (rare) when matters are widespread, (4) the Companions ignored it. Focus on the first.
These are the 'four aspects' mentioned.
3
Apply the first criterion: contradiction with Quran
Since the Quran is qat'i al-thubut, it cannot be set aside for a zanni report. This applies to all types of Quranic texts: specific/general, explicit/apparent.
The key rule: even the general (amm) of the Quran is not specified by khabar wahid according to Hanafis.
4
State the Hanafi restrictions on khabar wahid regarding Quran
Khabar wahid cannot: (a) specify a general verse, (b) add a ruling to the Quran, (c) abandon the apparent (zahir) meaning of the Quran, (d) abrogate the Quran. The Quranic text (matn) is the root and superior.
This is a concise list for memorization.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that general Quranic verses are zanni al-dalala and can be specified by a khabar wahid. This is the basis of ikhtilaf.
The dispute is about certainty of the general text's meaning, not transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الفصل الأخير فقد ردَّ بعض أهل الحديث الاتصال بالانقطاع، وعامتهم على أن الانقطاع يُجعل عفواً بالاتصال من وجه آخر. وأما الانقطاع الباطن : فنوعان : انقطاع بالمعارضة، وانقطاع لنقصان وقصور في الناقل. أما الأول : فإنما يظهر بالعرض على الأصول، فإذا خالف شيئاً ذلك : كان مردوداً منقطعاً، وذلك أربعة أوجه أيضاً: ما خالف كتاب الله تعالى. والثاني : ما خالف السنة المعروفة. والثالث : ما شد من الحديث فيما اشتهر من الحوادث، وعم به البلوى فورد مخالفاً للجماعة. والرابع: أن يُعرض عنه الأئمة من أصحاب النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام. أما الأول : فلأن الكتاب ثابت بيقين، فلا يترك بما فيه شبهة. ويستوي في ذلك الخاص والعام، والنص والظاهر، حتى إن العام من الكتاب لا يُخَص بخبر الواحد عندنا، وعند الشافعي يُخص. ولا يزاد على الكتاب بخبر الواحد عندنا. ولا يُترك الظاهر من الكتاب، ولا يُنسخُ بخبر الواحد وإن كان نصاً؛ لأن المتن أصل، والمعنى فرع له. والمتن من الكتاب : فوق المتن من السنَّة ؛ لثبوته ثبوتاً بلا شبهة فيه، فوجب الترجيح به قبل المصير إلى المعنى. وقد قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام : تكثر لكم الأحاديث من بعدي فإذا روي لكم عني حديث فاعرضوه على كتاب الله تعالى، فما وافق
As for the final chapter, some hadith scholars have rejected continuity (ittisal) due to discontinuity (inqita'), and their generality is that discontinuity is overlooked if there is continuity from another direction. As for hidden discontinuity (al-inqita' al-batin), it is of two types: discontinuity due to opposition (mu'arada), and discontinuity due to deficiency and shortcoming in the transmitter. As for the first, it becomes apparent by testing against the principles (usul). So if it contradicts something of those, it is rejected as disconnected. And that is also of four aspects: (1) what contradicts the Book of Allah; (2) what contradicts the known Sunnah; (3) what is rare (shadhdh) from the hadith in matters that are widely known among the people and general affliction (bala') and comes in opposition to the majority; (4) that the leading Companions (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) turn away from it. As for the first, because the Book is established with certainty, so it is not abandoned for something that has doubt. And in that, the specific and the general, the text (nass) and the apparent (zahir) are equal, such that the general of the Book is not specified by khabar wahid according to us, while according to al-Shafi'i it is specified. And nothing is added to the Book by khabar wahid according to us. Nor is the apparent of the Book abandoned, nor is it abrogated by khabar wahid even if it is nass, because the text (matn) is the root, and the meaning is a branch of it. And the text from the Book is above the text from the Sunnah, because it is established with no doubt in it, so preference must be given to it before resorting to meaning. And the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) said: 'Hadiths will increase for you after me; so if a hadith is narrated to you from me, present it to the Book of Allah; whatever agrees...'
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage discusses hidden discontinuity (inqita' batin) in hadith, particularly due to contradiction with established principles. The author identifies two types: oppositional and due to transmitter deficiency. The oppositional type is detected by testing against four criteria: the Quran, known Sunnah, widespread practice, and the practice of the Companions. The first criterion—contradiction with the Quran—is elaborated. The Quran is definitive (qat'i), so it cannot be abandoned for something doubtful (zanni). This applies to both specific and general verses, and to explicit (nass) and apparent (zahir) texts. The passage states the Hanafi rule: the general of the Quran cannot be specified (takhsis) by khabar wahid (alone hadith), unlike the Shafi'i position. Also, nothing can be added to the Quran by khabar wahid, nor can the apparent meaning be abandoned or abrogated by khabar wahid, even if that hadith is explicit (nass). The reasoning is that the Quranic text is the root (asl), and meaning is subordinate. The Quran's text is superior to the Sunnah's text due to its certainty. The passage ends with a hadith instructing to compare narrations with the Quran.

Key Terms
انقطاع باطن (inqiṭāʿ bāṭin): Hidden discontinuity in a hadith, not apparent from the chain but from contradiction with established principles.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur.
تخصيص (takhṣīṣ): Restricting the general meaning of a text to a subset of its application.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, what is the rule regarding a khabar wahid that contradicts a general verse of the Quran?
A) The general verse is specified by the khabar wahid.
B) The khabar wahid is accepted and the verse is reinterpreted.
C) The general verse remains general and the khabar wahid is rejected as hidden discontinuity.
D) The khabar wahid is preferred because it is later.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the Quran is qat'i and a khabar wahid cannot specify, add to, or abrogate it; any hadith that contradicts the Quran is rejected as having hidden discontinuity (inqita' batin).

Rejecting Hadith that Contradicts the Quran: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Takhsis
Explaining the first type of disconnected hadith: contradiction with Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi rule that a general Quranic verse cannot be specified by a solitary hadith and explain the epistemological basis for this position.

Core Idea
The Quran is certain; a solitary hadith is speculative — certainty cannot be overridden by speculation.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul introduces a critical usul principle: a hadith that contradicts the Quran is rejected as 'disconnected.' But the real dispute lies in what counts as contradiction. The Hanafis hold that even specifying a general verse of the Quran via a solitary hadith is a form of contradiction because it overrides the Quran's certainty with a speculative source. Here, we explore the reasoning behind this rule and examine the opposing Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of disconnected hadith
The passage opens by listing four reasons a hadith is considered munqati' (disconnected). The first is contradiction with the Quran, which is our focus. Recognize the pattern.
The other three types are: contradicting well-known Sunnah, differing from widely accepted practice, and being abandoned by the Companions.
2
Understand the epistemological premise
The text states: 'because the Book is established with certainty, so it is not abandoned for something that has doubt.' This is the core premise: the Quran is qat'i, a solitary hadith is zanni. Grasp this logical hierarchy.
3
Apply the rule to specification (takhsis)
The text explicitly says: 'even to the point that the general of the Book is not specified by a solitary hadith according to us, but according to al-Shafi'i it is specified.' Note the exact phrase and the disagreement.
This is the main point of dispute.
4
Examine the supporting hadith
The author cites a hadith commanding presentation to the Quran. However, the commentator immediately declares it weak. Understand that this hadith is not the primary evidence but a supporting argument.
The principle stands on certainty vs speculation, not on this weak hadith.
5
Distinguish other operations
The passage also forbids adding to the Quran, abandoning its apparent meaning, or abrogating it with a solitary hadith. Each operation is prohibited for the same epistemological reason.
These are separate rulings but derive from the same principle.

أما الأول : فإنما يظهر بالعرض على الأصول، فإذا خالف شيئاً ذلك : كان مردوداً منقطعاً، وذلك أربعة أوجه أيضاً:

والرابع: أن يُعرض عنه الأئمة من أصحاب النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام.
أما الأول : فلأن الكتاب ثابت بيقين، فلا يترك بما فيه شبهة.
ويستوي في ذلك الخاص والعام، والنص والظاهر، حتى إن العام من الكتاب لا يُخَص بخبر الواحد عندنا، وعند الشافعي يُخص.
ولا يزاد على الكتاب بخبر الواحد عندنا.

والمتن من الكتاب : فوق المتن من السنَّة ؛ لثبوته ثبوتاً بلا شبهة فيه، فوجب الترجيح به قبل المصير إلى المعنى.
وقد قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام : تكثر لكم الأحاديث من بعدي فإذا روي لكم عني حديث فاعرضوه على كتاب الله تعالى، فما وافق كتاب الله تعالى فاقبلوه وما خالفه فردوه». ضعيفة.
(1) حديث تكثر لكم الأحاديث أخرجه البيهقي في «المدخل» بطرق كلها ضعيفة. قال الشارح: أورده البخاري في كتابه، قلت: هذا يوهم أنه في «الصحيح»، وليس كذلك، وإنما قال في التاريخ : قال إبراهيم بن طهمان عن ابن أبي ذئب عن سعيد المقبري عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : «ما سمعتُم عني من حديث تعرفونه: فصدقوه».
وقال يحيى بن آدم عن أبي هريرة قال البخاري هو وهم، ليس فيه أبو هريرة. وقال البخاري: قال لنا عبد الله بن صالح أنا بكر عن عمرو عن بكير عن عبد الملك بن سعيد حدثه عن عباس بن سهل عن أبي : إذا بلغكم عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ما يُعرف ويلين الجلد، فقد يقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الخير، ولا يقول إلا الخير. قال البخاري وهذا أصح يعني من رواية من روى عن أبي حميد أو عن أبي أسيد مرفوعاً، كما أخرجه أحمد، وهذا ليس حديث الكتاب.
وحاصل طرق الحديث وألفاظه عن أبي جعفر رفعه: «إن الحديث سيفشو عني، فما أتاكم عني يوافق القرآن فهو عني وما أتاكم عني يخالف القرآن: فليس عني». رواه البيهقي، وضعفه.
وعن علي رَفَعَه : «إنها تكون بعدي رواة يروون عني الحديث: فاعرضوا حديثهم على القرآن، فما وافق القرآن فحدثوا به، وما لم يوافق القرآن: فلا تأخذوا به». رواه الدارقطني وقال : صوابه مرسل.
قلت : ولا حجة فيه لمن تأمل.

Disconnection due to contradiction, and disconnection due to deficiency and shortcoming in the transmitter. As for the first: it only becomes apparent by presenting (the hadith) to the foundational sources. So if it contradicts something of that, it is rejected, disconnected. That is also of four types: that which contradicts the Book of Allah; the second: that which contradicts the well-known Sunnah; the third: that which differs from the hadith in matters widely known among the people and common trials, so it comes contradicting the majority; the fourth: that from which the imams among the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) turn away. As for the first: because the Book is established with certainty, so it is not abandoned for something that has doubt. The specific and general, the clear text and apparent text are equal in this, even to the point that the general of the Book is not specified by a solitary hadith according to us, but according to al-Shafi'i it is specified. And nothing is added to the Book by a solitary hadith according to us. And the apparent meaning of the Book is not abandoned, nor is it abrogated by a solitary hadith even if it is a clear text, because the text (matn) is the origin, and the meaning is subsidiary to it. And the text of the Book is above the text of the Sunnah, because its establishment is certain without any doubt, so it is necessary to prefer it before resorting to meaning. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Hadith will become abundant after me, so if a hadith is narrated to you from me, present it to the Book of Allah; what agrees with the Book of Allah, accept it, and what contradicts it, reject it.' (Weak). (1) The hadith 'Hadith will become abundant...' was narrated by al-Bayhaqi in al-Madkhal via chains all weak. The commentator said: al-Bukhari mentioned it in his book. I say: this gives the impression that it is in the Sahih, but it is not. Rather, he said in al-Tarikh: Ibrahim ibn Tahman from Ibn Abi Dhi'b from Sa'id al-Maqburi from the Prophet (saw): 'Whatever you hear from me of hadith that you recognize, believe it.' And Yahya ibn Adam from Abu Hurayrah: al-Bukhari said it is a mistake; there is no Abu Hurayrah in it. And al-Bukhari said: 'Abdullah ibn Salih told us, from Bakr from 'Amr from Bukayr from 'Abd al-Malik ibn Sa'id who narrated from 'Abbas ibn Sahl from Abu: If a hadith from the Prophet (saw) reaches you that is known and makes the skin soft, then the Prophet (saw) says good and only says good. Al-Bukhari said this is more authentic, meaning than the narration from Abu Humayd or Abu Usayd as marfu', as Ahmad narrated, and this is not the hadith of the book. The summary of the chains and wordings from Abu Ja'far marfu': 'Indeed hadith will spread from me; what comes to you from me agreeing with the Quran is from me, and what comes to you from me contradicting the Quran is not from me.' Narrated by al-Bayhaqi and he declared it weak. And from 'Ali marfu': 'There will be narrators after me who narrate hadith from me; present their hadith to the Quran; what agrees with the Quran, narrate it; what does not agree with the Quran, do not take it.' Narrated by al-Daraqutni who said: correct is mursal. I say: there is no proof in it for one who reflects. And from Abu Hurayrah marfu': 'There will come to you differing hadith from me; what comes to you agreeing with the Book of Allah and my Sunnah is from me; what comes to you contradicting the Book of Allah and my Sunnah is not from me.' Narrated by Ibn 'Adi and declared weak because of al-Talhi.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh discussion about 'munqati'' (disconnected) hadith, specifically the category that contradicts established sources. The author (Bazdawi) states that a hadith is considered disconnected (and thus rejected) if it contradicts any of four sources: the Quran, well-known Sunnah, widely accepted practice among the community, or the consensus of the Companions. The focus here is the first: contradicting the Quran. The reason is the Quran is certain (qat'i) in its transmission, whereas a solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid) is speculative (zanni). Therefore, the Quran cannot be abandoned for something doubtful. This applies equally to specific and general verses, and to clear (nass) and apparent (zahir) texts. The Hanafi position is that a general verse of the Quran cannot be specified by a khabar al-wahid, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i who allows specification. Similarly, nothing can be added to the Quran via a solitary hadith, nor can an apparent meaning of the Quran be abandoned or abrogated by a khabar al-wahid, even if the hadith is textually clear (nass). The reasoning is that the matn (text) is the primary source, and meaning derived from it is secondary. The Quranic text is superior to the hadith text because the Quran's transmission is certain beyond doubt. Hence, preference is given to the Quran before resorting to interpretative meaning. The author then cites a hadith reportedly from the Prophet commanding that hadith be presented to the Quran; those agreeing are accepted, those contradicting are rejected. However, the commentator (possibly the hashiya writer) notes that this hadith is weak, citing multiple chains and scholars like al-Bukhari and al-Bayhaqi who declared its weakness. This does not affect the principle, which is established by rational necessity and consensus. The dispute with al-Shafi'i is highlighted: al-Shafi'i permits specifying the general of the Quran with a khabar al-wahid, whereas the Hanafis require certainty (Quran or mutawatir) for specification. This difference stems from usul: Hanafis consider 'amm as qat'i until specified, while Shafi'is consider it zanni.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.
عام (amm): A word that encompasses all individuals or items of its category without restriction.
متن (matn): The text of a scriptural source (Quran or hadith) as opposed to its derived meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it can specify just like a verse of the Quran.
B) No, because the Quran is certain and a solitary hadith is speculative.
C) Yes, but only if the hadith is narrated by trustworthy narrators.
D) No, because only the Sunnah can specify the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a general Quranic verse cannot be specified by a solitary hadith because the Quran is certain (qat'i) and a solitary hadith is speculative (zanni); certainty must not be overridden by speculation.

Khabar al-Wahid Cannot Abrogate the Qur'an – The Hanafi Principle
Stating Hanafi principle on accepting khabar al-wahid without naskh of Qur'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that khabar al-wahid cannot abrogate the Qur'an to evaluate whether a given hadith can override a Qur'anic ruling.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid is zanni; the Qur'an is qat'i – the weaker cannot abrogate the stronger.

In this passage, the Hanafi school sets out a foundational rule for dealing with prophetic reports that appear to conflict with the Qur'an. The text rejects both extremes: rejecting all ahad reports, and accepting them uncritically even when they contradict the Book. Instead, it stakes out a middle path: grant each proof its proper weight. We will unpack this principle and see how it applies to classic examples like the hadith of touching the penis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two extreme positions rejected
The text rejects those who reject all khabar al-ahad (leading to reliance on weak proofs like qiyas or istishab) and those who accept them to abrogate the Qur'an (destroying certainty).
These extremes are: total rejection vs. uncritical acceptance.
2
State the Hanafi middle position
Khabar al-wahid is accepted as a valid proof, but it cannot abrogate the Qur'an. It is used only in matters not already ruled by a definitive text.
The phrase 'تنزيل كل دليلٍ منزلتَه' – giving each evidence its proper rank.
3
Analyze the epistemological basis
The Qur'an is qat'i (definitive) in both transmission (thubut) and meaning (dalalah). Khabar al-wahid is zanni (speculative) in both. The definitive cannot be overridden by the speculative.
This is a core Hanafi usul principle.
4
Apply to the given examples
The hadith about touching the penis is rejected because it contradicts the Qur'anic praise of those who perform istinja' (which involves touching). The second example (Fatima bint Qays) is said to similarly conflict.
The example illustrates the principle in action.
5
Distinguish between bayan and naskh
Explanation (bayan) of the Qur'an by khabar al-wahid is allowed – it clarifies without abrogating. Abrogation (naskh) requires evidence of equal or greater certainty.
This nuance is key to understanding the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلذلك نقول: إنه لا يُقبل خبر الواحد في نسخ الكتاب، ويُقبل فيما ليس في كتاب الله على وجه لا ينسخه. ومن ردَّ أخبار الآحاد فقد أبطل الحجة، فوقع في العمل بالشبهة، وهو القياس، أو استصحاب الحال الذي ليس بحجة أصلاً. ومن عمل بالآحاد على مخالفة الكتاب ونَسْخه : فقد أبطل اليقين، والأولُ فَتَحَ باب الجهل والإلحاد، والثاني فتح باب البدعة، وإنما سواء السبيل فيما قاله أصحابنا رحمهم الله في تنزيل كل دليلٍ منزلتَه. ومثال هذا حديث مس الذكر : أنه يخالف الكتاب؛ لأن الله تعالى مدح المتطهرين بالاستنجاء بقوله: ﴿ فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَن يَنطَهَرُوا ﴾ [التوبة:108]، والمستنجي يمس ذكره، وهو بمنزلة البول عند من جعله حدثاً. ومثل حديث فاطمة بنت قيس الذي روينا في النفقة : أنه يخالف
Therefore we say: A khabar al-wahid (single-narrator report) is not accepted for abrogation of the Book, but is accepted in what is not in the Book of Allah in a manner that does not abrogate it. And whoever rejects khabar al-ahad (reports of single narrators) has invalidated the proof, thus falling into acting upon doubt, which is qiyas (analogy) or istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity) which is not a proof at all. And whoever acts upon khabar al-ahad in opposition to and abrogation of the Book has invalidated certainty. The first opened the door of ignorance and heresy, and the second opened the door of innovation. The middle path is what our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) said: giving every proof its proper rank. An example of this is the hadith of touching the penis: it contradicts the Book because Allah Almighty praised those who purify themselves with istinja' (cleansing after relieving oneself) by His saying: 'In it are men who love to purify themselves' [al-Tawbah:108], and the one who performs istinja' touches his penis, and it is like urine according to those who consider it an invalidator of wudu. And similarly the hadith of Fatima bint Qays which we narrated concerning maintenance: it contradicts...
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi principle regarding the acceptance of khabar al-wahid (a report transmitted by one or a few narrators). The author asserts that such reports cannot abrogate a ruling derived from the Qur'an. However, they are accepted in matters not explicitly mentioned in the Qur'an, provided they do not contradict or abrogate it. The text then criticizes two extreme positions: first, those who reject all khabar al-ahad, thereby losing a valid proof and falling into reliance on weak substitutes like qiyas or istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity). Second, those who accept khabar al-ahad even when they oppose the Qur'an and attempt to abrogate it, thus destroying certainty. The Hanafi middle path is to give each evidence its appropriate weight. Two examples follow: the hadith about touching the penis causing wudu to break is rejected because it contradicts the Qur'anic praise of those who perform istinja' (which involves touching). The second example, the hadith of Fatima bint Qays regarding maintenance, is said to contradict the Qur'an, though the passage cuts off before completing the argument. This reflects the Hanafi usul principle that khabar al-wahid is zanni (speculative) and cannot abrogate the qat'i (definitive) Qur'an.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a previous legal ruling by a later one.
استصحاب الحال (istishab al-hal): Presumption of continuity of a legal state until evidence of change.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is accepted and the Qur'an is abrogated.
B) It is rejected because the Qur'an is definitive and khabar al-wahid is speculative.
C) It is rejected only if it comes from a weak narrator.
D) It is accepted and the Qur'an is interpreted allegorically.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts khabar al-wahid as a proof but denies its ability to abrogate the Qur'an due to the difference in epistemic certainty.

Conditions for Accepting Reports: Agents vs Volunteers
Analyzing conditions of 'adalah and 'adad in accepting reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for accepting reports from a volunteer (fuduli) and identify the conditions of 'adalah and 'adad according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A volunteer's report requires either one just informant or two, because it sits between binding rights and transactions.

In Hanafi usul, the conditions for accepting a legal report depend on who delivers it. An agent or messenger is trusted by virtue of his appointment, but a volunteer (fuduli) who reports on his own initiative triggers a debate. Should the report be treated like testimony, requiring integrity and number? Or like a transaction, where any reporter suffices? This passage presents the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, showing a middle path.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of informant
Read the first line: if the informant is an agent (wakil) or messenger (rasul) of the recipient, no condition of 'adalah is needed. This is because he stands in place of the recipient and is already trustworthy in that role.
This rule is simple and uncontested.
2
Distinguish the volunteer's case
When a volunteer (fuduli) reports on his own initiative, the conditions change. The text then presents Abu Hanifa's view and the Sahibayn's view. Identify the core disagreement: number and integrity requirements.
3
State Abu Hanifa's conditions
Abu Hanifa requires either a single just reporter ('adl) or two reporters without requiring both to be 'adl. The phrase 'the report of a slave, boy, and woman is not accepted' indicates that if only one reporter, he must be 'adl; if two, 'adalah is not necessary.
This is a middle ground between testimony and transaction.
4
Understand the Sahibayn's position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, all reporters are equal because the matter is purely from transactions (mu'amalat). Thus, reports from slaves, boys, and women are accepted equally to free adults.
Their view eliminates special conditions.
5
Grasp the talil (reasoning) of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the volunteer's report is like binding rights in one respect (it can lead to removal or interdiction) but like transactions in another respect (the annulment acts in his own right). Therefore, it sits 'between two stations' (bayna manzilatayn), so either number or integrity suffices.
This talil explains the middle position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا كان المبلغ وكيلاً أو رسولاً ممن إليه الإبلاغ: لم تشترط فيه العدالة؛ لأنه قائم مقام غيره. وإذا أخبره فضولي بنفسه مبتدئاً : فإن أبا حنيفة رحمه الله قال: لا يُقبل فيه إلا خبر الواحد العدل. وفي الاثنين: كذلك عند بعضهم. وقال بعضهم : لا تشترط العدالة في الاثنين. ولفظ «الكتاب في الاثنين محتمل، فإن محمداً رحمه الله قال: حتى يخبره رجل واحد عدل، أو رجلان، ولم تشترط العدالة فيهما نصاً. ويحتمل أن تُشترط سائر شرائط الشهادة، إلا العدد عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، أو العددَ مع سائر الشرائط غير العدالة، فلا يقبل خبر العبد والصبي والمرأة. فأما عندهما : فإن الكل سواء؛ لأنه من باب المعاملات. ولكن أبا حنيفة رحمه الله قال : إنه من جنس الحقوق اللازمة من وجه ؛ لأنه يلزمه حكماً بالعزل والحجر، يلزمه فيه العهدة، من لزوم عقد، أو فساد عمل. ومن وجه يُشبه سائر المعاملات ؛ لأن الذي يفسخ : يتصرف في حقه، كما يتصرف فيه بالإطلاق، فشَرَطنا فيه العددَ، أو العدالة؛ لكونها بين منزلتين. بخلاف المخبر إذا كان رسولاً؛ لما قلنا. وفي شرط الاثنين من غير عدالة على ما قاله بعض مشايخنا رحمهم الله فائدة لتوكيد الحجة، وللعدد تأثير في التوكيد بلا إشكال، والله أعلم. والتزكية من القسم الرابع عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله ، وقال محمد رحمه الله هو من جنس القسم الثالث، على ما عرف، والله أعلم.
If the informant is an agent or messenger of the person to whom he is reporting, integrity is not required in him because he stands in place of another. And if a volunteer informs him on his own initiative, Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Only the report of a single just person is accepted in it. And regarding two, likewise according to some of them. And some said: Integrity is not required in the case of two. And the wording of the book regarding two is ambiguous, for Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: until a single just man or two men inform him, and he did not explicitly stipulate integrity in the case of two. And it is possible that all other conditions of testimony are required, except number according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), or number along with all conditions other than integrity, so the report of a slave, a boy, and a woman is not accepted. As for according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), all are the same because it is from the category of transactions. But Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is from the category of binding rights in one respect, because it binds him by a ruling of removal and interdiction, and he bears responsibility therein, from the binding of a contract or corruption of an act. And in another respect it resembles other transactions because the one who annuls acts in his right as he acts in it absolutely, so we stipulated number or integrity because it is between two ranks. Contrary to the informant when he is a messenger, as we said. And in stipulating two without integrity, as some of our teachers (may Allah have mercy on them) said, there is a benefit of strengthening the proof, and number has an effect in strengthening without doubt, and Allah knows best. And tazkiyah is from the fourth category according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them), and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said it is from the third category, as known, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule discussing the conditions for accepting reports (akhbar) in legal matters, specifically the requirement of 'adalah (integrity) and 'adad (number). The author begins by stating that if the informant is an agent (wakil) or messenger (rasul) of the person being informed, no condition of integrity is required because he acts as a representative. Then the discussion turns to a voluntary informant (fuduli) who initiates contact. Abu Hanifa imposes strict conditions: only the report of a single just person is accepted. On the issue of two informants, there is disagreement: some require integrity for both, while others dispense with it. The author notes that Muhammad al-Shaybani's wording is ambiguous; he explicitly required integrity for one but not for two, and did not specify for two. The author considers the possibility that all conditions of testimony (except number according to Abu Hanifa) apply, so reports from slaves, boys, and women are rejected. In contrast, the Two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider all such reports equal because they pertain to transactions (mu'amalat), where such conditions are not required. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is nuanced: voluntary reports are similar in one aspect to binding rights (like removal or interdiction) because they produce legal consequences, but in another aspect they resemble transactions. Therefore, he requires either number or integrity, as a middle ground. The passage ends with a statement about tazkiyah (verification of witnesses): Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf classify it in the fourth category, while Muhammad places it in the third, showing further internal ijtihad within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المبلغ (al-muballigh): The informant who conveys a report to someone.
الوكيل (al-wakīl): An agent appointed to act on behalf of another.
الرسول (al-rasūl): A messenger who delivers a message without independent authority.
الفضولي (al-fuḍūlī): A volunteer who acts on behalf of another without prior appointment.
العدالة (al-ʿadālah): Moral integrity and legal reliability, a condition for testimony and reports.
العدد (al-ʿadad): Number of reporters (typically two, like witnesses).
التزكية (al-tazkiyah): Verification of a witness's integrity by the court or authorized persons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on accepting a report from a volunteer (fuduli) under Abu Hanifa's view?
A) It is accepted only if the reporter is a single just person or two persons without requiring 'adalah.
B) It is accepted from any reporter because it is a transaction.
C) It is accepted only from an agent or messenger.
D) It is never accepted because a volunteer has no standing.

Key Takeaway
The conditions for accepting a report depend on the role of the informant: agents and messengers require no 'adalah, while volunteers are subject to either number or integrity due to their mixed legal nature.

The General Concession for Narrating Hadith by Meaning
Ruling on narrating hadith by meaning with ijma evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on narrating hadith by meaning and explain the ijma proof that supports it.

Core Idea
Narrating hadith by meaning is a concession (rukhsa) based on Companion consensus; the wording is not like the Quran.

The passage opens by stating the majority view—including the Hanafis—that narrating hadith by meaning is permissible as a facilitation. This is supported by the consensus of the Companions who would report the Prophet’s commands using approximations. The author distinguishes this from the Quran, whose miraculous nature lies in its exact wording. This lesson explores the evidential basis (dalil) for this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
State that narrating by meaning is a rukhsa (concession) according to the majority. The basis is ijma of the Companions, who used phrases like 'or something similar' when transmitting hadith.
This ijma is considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
2
Examine the dalil al-ijma
The Companions' practice of reporting the Prophet's words with approximations shows they considered the meaning sufficient. The text explicitly cites their consensus: 'the consensus of the Companions on their saying: The Messenger of God commanded us such-and-such... or something similar.'
This is not a textual dalil but an ijma proof.
3
Contrast with the Quran
The rationale for the concession is that the Quran's composition (nazm) is inimitable and its wording is miraculous, whereas the Sunnah's authority lies in its meaning. Thus, narrating by meaning is permissible for hadith but not for Quran.
This distinction is crucial for the ruling.
4
Note the limitation
The concession is not absolute; it is restricted later in the passage based on the type of hadith text. The general principle applies only to unambiguous texts (muhkam) and for qualified scholars.
The passage later qualifies the concession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال عامة العلماء: لا بأس بذلك في الجملة رخصة؛ لاتفاق الصحابة على قولهم: أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بكذا، ونهانا عن كذا، أو نحواً منه، أو قريباً منه. وفي تفصيل الرخصة جواب عما قال، وهذا لأن النظم من قرآن معجز، وإنما النظم لمعناه، بخلاف القرآن.
والسنة في هذا الباب أنواع:
ما يكون محكماً لا يشتبه معناه، ولا يحتمل غير ما وضع له.
وظاهر يحتمل غير ما ظهر من معناه، من عام يحتمل الخصوص، أو حقيقة تحتمل المجاز.
ومشكل، أو مشترك لا يعمل به إلا بتأويل.
ومجمل، أو متشابه.
وقد يكون من جوامع الكلم التي اختص بها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم.
قال عليه الصلاة والسلام فيما يحكي من اختصاصه: "وأوتيت جوامع الكلم".
فهي خمسة أقسام:
أما الأول: فلا بأس لمن له بصر بوجوه اللغة أن ينقله إلى لفظ يؤدي معناه؛ لأنه إذا كان محكماً مفسراً: أمن فيه الغلط على أهل العلم بوجوه اللغة، فثبت النقل رخصةً وتيسيراً، وقد ثبت في كتاب الله تعالى ضرب من الرخصة مع أن النظم معجز.
قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: أنزل القرآن على سبعة أحرف. وإنما ثبت ذلك ببركة دعوة النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام، غير أن ذلك رخصة إسقاط، وهذه رخصة تخفيف وتيسير مع قيام الأصل، على نحو ما مرَّ تقسيمه في باب العزيمة والرخصة.
وأما القسم الثاني: فلا رخصة فيه إلا لمن حوى إلى علم اللغة فقه
And the majority of scholars said: There is no harm in that in general as a concession, due to the consensus of the Companions on their saying: 'The Messenger of God commanded us such-and-such and forbade us such-and-such' or something similar or close to it. And in the detailed treatment of the concession is a response to what was said, and this is because the composition (of the Quran) is inimitable, yet the composition is for its meaning, unlike the Quran.
And the Sunnah in this regard are types:
- What is muhkam, whose meaning is not ambiguous, and does not admit anything other than what it was placed for.
- And what is zahir, which admits other than what is apparent from its meaning, such as a general that admits specification, or a literal that admits metaphor.
- And what is mushkil or mushtarak, which is not acted upon except with interpretation.
- And what is mujmal or mutashabih.
- And it may be from the comprehensive words (jawami' al-kalim) with which the Messenger was uniquely endowed.
He said in reporting his distinction: 'I have been given the comprehensive words.'
Thus they are five divisions:
As for the first: There is no objection for one who has insight into aspects of language to transmit it into an expression that conveys its meaning, because when it is muhkam and clearly explained, error is safe from the people of knowledge of language. So transmission is established as a concession and facilitation, and there is established in the Book of God a kind of concession even though its composition is inimitable.
The Prophet said: 'The Quran was revealed in seven letters.' That was established by the blessing of the Prophet's supplication, but that was a concession of abrogation, while this is a concession of alleviation and facilitation along with the principle remaining, according to the classification previously mentioned in the chapter on determination and concession.
And as for the second division: There is no concession in it except for one who has, in addition to linguistics, jurisprudence...
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bazdawi's usul work addresses the permissibility of narrating hadith by meaning (al-riwaya bi al-ma'na). The author begins by presenting the majority view that it is permissible as a concession (rukhsa), citing the consensus of the Companions who would often report the Prophet's words with approximations like 'or something similar.' This is because the miraculous element of the Quran lies in its precise wording, whereas the Sunnah's authority is in its meaning, not its exact wording. 

He then classifies the Sunnah texts into five categories based on their clarity: 
1. Muhkam: unequivocal, not open to other interpretations. 
2. Zahir: apparent but may admit specification or metaphorical interpretation. 
3. Mushkil/Mushtarak: problematic or homonymous, requiring interpretation. 
4. Mujmal/Mutashabih: ambiguous or similar, often not definitively understood. 
5. Jawami' al-kalim: comprehensive concise speech, a special gift to the Prophet. 

For each category, he discusses the permissibility of narrating by meaning. For the first (muhkam), it is allowed for a qualified linguist because there is no risk of error. He compares it to the Quranic concession of recitation in seven letters, which was a temporary license. For the second (zahir), he begins stating that it is not permissible except for one who combines linguistic knowledge with fiqh (deep understanding). The passage appears to be cut off, indicating the importance of further qualification in such cases.

Key Terms
رخصة (rukhsa): A concession or license that allows what would otherwise be prohibited or restricted, due to necessity or ease.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahid scholars of the ummah on a legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence cited in the passage for the permissibility of narrating hadith by meaning?
A) A Quranic verse
B) A prophetic hadith
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Qiyas on the Quran

Key Takeaway
Narrating hadith by meaning is a concession based on Companion consensus, but it is restricted to unambiguous texts and qualified narrators.

Classification of Sunnah Texts and the Ruling for Muhkam
Classification of Sunnah texts and ruling for muhkam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a sunnah text into one of five categories based on clarity, and explain the ruling on narrating it by meaning for the muhkam category.

Core Idea
Only unambiguous texts (muhkam) can be narrated by meaning freely; ambiguous texts require deeper knowledge or are prohibited.

The author provides a systematic classification of Sunnah texts according to their semantic clarity, from muhkam (unequivocal) down to mujmal and mutashabih (ambiguous). For each type, the permissibility of narrating by meaning differs. This lesson focuses on the categories and the specific ruling for muhkam texts, which are the safest to transmit by meaning.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the five categories
List and memorize: 1) Muhkam, 2) Zahir, 3) Mushkil/Mushtarak, 4) Mujmal/Mutashabih, 5) Jawami' al-Kalim.
These are based on increasing ambiguity.
2
Define each category using the text
Muhkam: meaning is not ambiguous. Zahir: apparent meaning but admits takhsis or metaphor. Mushkil/Mushtarak: requires interpretation. Mujmal/Mutashabih: ambiguous, not clear without bayan. Jawami' al-Kalim: concise comprehensive speech unique to the Prophet.
The passage groups mujmal and mutashabih together.
3
Identify the ruling for muhkam
The passage explicitly states that for muhkam texts, a person with linguistic insight may narrate by meaning without restriction, because error is avoided.
This is the most permissive category.
4
Note the incomplete ruling for zahir
The text begins the ruling for zahir but is cut off. It says 'no concession except for one who has, in addition to linguistics, jurisprudence (fiqh).' This implies additional qualifications are needed.
The passage is truncated; we infer that a stricter condition applies.

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bazdawi's usul work addresses the permissibility of narrating hadith by meaning (al-riwaya bi al-ma'na). The author begins by presenting the majority view that it is permissible as a concession (rukhsa), citing the consensus of the Companions who would often report the Prophet's words with approximations like 'or something similar.' The passage appears to be cut off, indicating the importance of further qualification in such cases.

Key Terms
محكم (muhkam): A textual expression whose meaning is unambiguous and does not admit any other interpretation.
ظاهر (zahir): An expression that is apparent in meaning but may admit specification (takhsis) or metaphorical interpretation.
مشكل (mushkil): A problematic expression that is not clear without interpretation, often due to ambiguity or homonymy.
مجمل (mujmal): An ambiguous expression that cannot be understood without elaboration (bayan).
جوامع الكلم (jawami' al-kalim): Concise expressions that convey comprehensive meanings, a miracle given to the Prophet.

According to the passage, which type of sunnah text is described as 'not acting upon it except with interpretation'?
A) Muhkam
B) Zahir
C) Mushkil or Mushtarak
D) Mujmal or Mutashabih

Key Takeaway
The five types of Sunnah texts differ in clarity; only muhkam texts are unconditionally safe for meaning transmission by a qualified linguist.

Denial by the Narrated Authority: An Intra-Hanafi Usul Dispute
Listing four types of criticism and analysing the denial dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on the effect of a narrator's denial of his own narration and apply the underlying qiyas principle (judge-witness analogy) to similar usul disputes.

Core Idea
When a narrator denies his report, Hanafis differ: is the hadith dropped? The answer hinges on whether doubt invalidates a testimony.

The reliability of hadith is not only about the chain's integrity but also about the narrator's own stance. Imam al-Bazdawi, in his Usul, addresses a critical scenario: what happens when the very person from whom a hadith is reported (e.g., a Companion) denies ever narrating it? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi internal disagreement, its basis in a qiyas from judicial testimony, and the prophetic precedent from the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn. By the end, you will grasp how doubt and certainty interact in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Types of Narrator Criticism
Al-Bazdawi lists four ways a narrator can invalidate a hadith: explicit rejection, acting contrary, specification/interpretation, and refraining from action. Read the first part of the passage and note each type.
The third type is textually corrupt; focus on the fourth as it leads to the main dispute.
2
Isolate the Disputed Scenario: Denial by the Authority
The fourth type—when the one narrated from denies the narration—is the core issue. The Salaf differed; identify both positions: action dropped vs. not dropped.
Al-Bazdawi says 'this is more appropriate' (وهذا أشبه) for dropping, but the dispute remains.
3
Map the Hanafi Ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Within the Hanafi school, Abu Yusuf holds that such a hadith is dropped for argumentation; Muhammad holds it is not dropped. Trace this back to their difference on a judge who does not recall a case when two witnesses testify.
This is a classic example of intra-madhhab ikhtilaf rooted in a qiyas principle.
4
Analyze the Dalil: The Hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn
The passage cites the hadith where the Prophet did not immediately accept Dhu al-Yadayn's report but consulted Abu Bakr and Umar. Evaluate how this supports Muhammad's view: the report was not rejected outright, but confirmation was sought.
Note the disclaimer at the end about hand placement—irrelevant to the legal point.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: if a Companion denies a hadith, should a mujtahid still use it? Abu Yusuf says no, Muhammad says yes. Which view is more cautious, and which is more open to evidence?
The author's preference for dropping action suggests a cautious approach.

باب وما يلحقه النكيرُ من قِبَل الراوي ولهذا النوع أربعة أقسام : ١ ـ ما أنكره صريحاً. ٢ والثاني : أن يعمل بخلافه قبل أن يبلغه، أو بعد ما بلغه، أو لا يُعرف تاريخه. ٣- تخصيص. والقسم الثالث: أن يُعين بعض ما احتمله الحديث من تأويل أو [؟] والرابع: أن يمتنع عن العمل به. أما إذا أنكر المروي عنه الرواية، فقد اختلف فيه السلف : فقال بعضهم: لا يسقط العمل به. وقال بعضهم : يسقط العمل به، وهذا أشبه. وقد قيل : إن قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله : أن يسقط الاحتجاج به، وقال محمد رحمه الله : لا يسقط. وهو فرع اختلافهما في شاهدين شَهِدا على القاضي بقضية، وهو لا يذكرها : فقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : لا تُقبل، وقال محمد رحمه الله : تُقبل. أما مَن قَبلَه : فقد احتج بما روي في حديث ذي اليدين: أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام لم يقبل خبره ، وقال لأبي بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما: «ماذا يقول ذو اليدين؟» حتى أخبراه. وليس المسلم وضع اليد، ولا التشبيك.
Chapter: What attaches to criticism from the side of the narrator. This type has four divisions: 1) What he explicitly rejected. 2) The second: that he acts contrary to it before it reaches him, or after it reaches him, or its date is not known. 3) Specification. The third division: that it specifies some of what the hadith admits of interpretation or [?]. The fourth: that he refrains from acting upon it. As for when the one narrated from denies the narration, the Salaf differed about it: some said: action by it is not dropped. And some said: action by it is dropped, and this is more appropriate. And it has been said: the view of Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, is that argumentation by it is dropped, and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: it is not dropped. This is a branch of their disagreement regarding two witnesses who testified before a judge regarding a case while he does not remember it: Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said: they are not accepted, and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: they are accepted. As for what precedes it: he adduced as proof what is narrated in the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn: that the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, did not accept his news, and he said to Abu Bakr and Umar, may Allah be pleased with them: 'What does Dhu al-Yadayn say?' until they informed him. And it is not the placing of the hand, nor the interlacing of fingers.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is from the usul al-fiqh work of al-Bazdawi, discussing a rule regarding the acceptance of hadith. The author first lists four types of criticism that can attach to a hadith from the narrator's side: (1) explicit rejection by the narrator himself, (2) acting contrary to the hadith before or after it reaches him, or if the date of his action is unknown, (3) specifying some interpretation or specification that the hadith admits, and (4) refraining from acting upon it. Then the focus shifts to a specific scenario: when the person from whom the hadith is narrated (the authority, e.g., a Companion) denies having narrated it. The earlier scholars (Salaf) differed: some said the hadith remains valid and action is not dropped, while others said action is dropped. The author notes that the latter view is more appropriate. Within the Hanafi school, there is a famous difference: Abu Yusuf holds that such a hadith is no longer valid for argumentation (i.e., it is rejected), while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it remains valid. This ikhtilaf is derived from their disagreement about a case where two witnesses testify before a judge about a case he does not remember: Abu Yusuf does not accept their testimony because the judge's lack of memory casts doubt, while Muhammad accepts it because the witnesses' testimony is independent. The passage then provides a proof for the view that the authority's denial does not automatically invalidate the hadith: the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn (the incident of forgetful prayer). In that hadith, when Dhu al-Yadayn informed the Prophet that he had prayed only two rak'ahs, the Prophet did not immediately accept his single report but asked Abu Bakr and Umar to confirm. This shows that the Prophet did not reject the news outright; rather, he sought corroboration. The final sentence 'وليس المسلم وضع اليد، ولا التشبيك' seems to correct a common misunderstanding that the hadith contains details about hand placement or finger interlacing, which are not part of the core ruling.

Key Terms
النكير من قبل الراوي (al-nakīr min qibali al-rāwī): Criticism that attaches to a hadith due to issues related to the narrator himself (as opposed to the text).
إنكار المروي عنه (inkār al-marwī ʿanhu): Denial by the person from whom the hadith is reported (e.g., a Companion) that he narrated it.
حديث ذي اليدين (ḥadīth Dhī al-Yadayn): The hadith about the man named Dhu al-Yadayn who alerted the Prophet during the forgetful prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the view of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding a hadith when the authority from whom it is narrated denies it?
A) The hadith is dropped and cannot be used for argumentation.
B) The hadith is not dropped and remains valid for argumentation.
C) The hadith is accepted only if it is mutawatir.
D) The hadith is accepted only if the authority is a Companion.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains a legitimate internal ikhtilaf on whether a narrator's denial invalidates his hadith; the dispute mirrors the judge-witness analogy and highlights the tension between doubt and certainty in usul al-fiqh.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Narrator's Interpretation Does Not Invalidate Other Meanings: A Hanafi Usul Principle
Usul rule with two illustrative examples and a cross-madhhab objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that a narrator's interpretation of a general text does not eliminate its other possible meanings, and evaluate its impact on takhsis.

Core Idea
A narrator's acting on one meaning does not reject others — linguistic possibility remains.

This lesson introduces a key Hanafi usul principle: when a Companion narrates a hadith and then acts upon one of its possible meanings, the other meanings are not thereby invalidated. This principle protects the generality of texts from being prematurely narrowed by personal interpretation. We will examine two examples: Ibn Umar's understanding of 'separation' in the sale option hadith, and Ibn Abbas's ruling on the female apostate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The passage states that acting on one possible meaning does not prove a defect or reject others. Recognise this as the core usul rule.
The principle is based on linguistic possibility (ihtimal) not being invalidated by ta'wil.
2
Analyse the linguistic basis
Understand the terms ihtimal (possibility) and ishtirak (homonymy). Homonymy is not undone by a narrator's interpretation.
Ishtirak is a type of ihtimal but specifically for words with multiple distinct meanings.
3
Apply to the first example: Ibn Umar
Ibn Umar interpreted 'tafarruq' as physical separation. The hadith also permits separation by words. His interpretation does not invalidate the other meaning.
The word is mushtarak; meaning remains open for other evidence.
4
Apply to the second example: Ibn Abbas
Ibn Abbas specified the general command 'kill whoever changes his religion' to males only. This specification does not negate the general applicability for males.
The generality remains intact; Ibn Abbas's ruling is a valid takhsis.
5
Evaluate the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argued that a Companion's statement cannot override a general marfu' hadith. The Hanafi response is implied: the Companion's interpretation is a valid bayan, not a rejection.
The dispute shows the practical impact: female apostates are killed in Shafi'i fiqh but not in Hanafi.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عمل الراوي ببعض محتملاته: فرد لسائر الوجوه، لكنه لا يثبت الجرح بهذا؛ لأن احتمال الكلام لغةً: لا يبطل بتأويله.
وذلك مثل حديث ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما: «المتبايعان بالخيار ما لم يتفرقا»، وحَمَلَه على افتراق الأبدان والحديث يحتمل افتراق الأقوال، وهو بمعنى المشترك؛ لأنهما معنيان مختلفان والاشتراك لغةً لا يَسقط بتأويله.
(۱) حديث ابن عمر عن عبد بن عمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: البيعان بالخيار ما لم يتفرقا أو يقول أحدهما لصاحبه اختر، وربما قال أو يكون بيع الخيار.
وفي لفظ: إذا تبايع الرجلان فكل واحد منهما بالخيار ما لم يتفرقا، وكانا جميعاً، أو يخير أحدهما الآخر، فإن خير أحدهما الآخر فتبايعا على ذلك: فقد وجب البيع، وإن تفرقا بعد أن تبايعا ولم يترك واحد منهما البيع فقد وجب البيع. متفق على ذلك كله.
وفي لفظ: «كل بيعين لا بيع بينهما حتى يتفرقا إلا الخيار». متفق عليه أيضاً.
وفي لفظ: المتبايعان كل واحد منهما بالخيار على صاحبه ما لم يتفرقا، إلا الخيار.
وفي لفظ: «إذا تبايع المتبايعان بالبيع فكل واحد منهما بالخيار من بيعه ما لم يتفرقا، أو يكون بيعهما عن خيار، فإذا كان بيعهما عن خيار فقد وجب البيع. قال نافع: «وكان عبد الله بن عمر رحمهما الله إذا أراد أن يبايع رجلاً، فأراد أن لا يُقيله: قام فمشى هنية، ثم رجع». أخرجاهما.
وهذا أراد المصنِّفُ بقوله: حَمَلَه على افتراق الأبدان.
ومن ذلك حديث عبد الله بن عباس رضي الله عنهما: «مَن بدل دينه فاقتلوه(۱) وقال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما: لا تُقتل المرتدة (٢).
وقال الشافعي رحمه الله: لا يُترَك عموم الحديث بقوله وتخصيصه، والامتناع عن العمل به مثل العمل بخلافه؛ لأن الامتناع حرام، مثل العمل بخلافه، والله أعلم.
(۱) حديث ابن عباس عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن بدل دينه فاقتلوه لفظ ابن ماجه وأخرجه البخاري وبقية أصحاب السنن في قصة.
(۲) قوله: وقال ابن عباس: لا تُقتل المرتدة أخرج ابن أبي شيبة حدثنا عبد الرحيم بن سليمان ووكيع عن أبي حنيفة عن عاصم عن أبي رزين عن ابن عباس قال: لا تقتل النساء إذا ارتددن عن الإسلام، ولكن يُحبسن ويُدعَين إلى الإسلام، ويُجبرن عليه»، وأخرجه الدارقطني من طريق أبي مالك النخعي عن عاصم قلت: وقد قالوا: محلَّ هذا: إذا لم يكن المرفوع عاماً، وهذا المرفوع عام، فأَنَّى يستقيم؟ والله أعلم.
As for the narrator acting on some of its possible meanings: that is a rejection of the other aspects, but it does not establish defect by this; because the linguistic possibility of speech is not invalidated by its interpretation. And that is like the hadith of Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both: 'The two parties to a sale have the option as long as they have not separated', and he interpreted it as separation of bodies, while the hadith can also mean separation by words, and it is like the common term (mushtarak) because they are two different meanings, and linguistic commonality is not dropped by its interpretation. (1) The hadith of Ibn Umar from Abd ibn Umar: the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The two sellers have the option as long as they have not separated or one of them says to his companion: Choose', and sometimes he said: 'or it is a sale with option.' And in another wording: 'When two men transact a sale, each of them has the option as long as they have not separated and both are together, or one gives the other the choice; if one gives the other the choice and they transact on that, then the sale is binding, and if they separate after transacting and neither has left the sale, then the sale is binding.' Agreed upon on all that. And in another wording: 'No sale between two sellers until they separate except the option.' Also agreed upon. And in another wording: 'The two parties to a sale each have the option over his companion as long as they have not separated except the option.' And in another wording: 'When the two parties transact a sale, each of them has the option regarding his sale as long as they have not separated, or their sale is based on option; if their sale is based on option, then the sale is binding.' Nafi' said: 'Abdullah ibn Umar, may Allah have mercy on them both, when he wanted to transact with a man and wanted not to give him the right of cancellation, he would stand and walk a little, then return.' Both reported. And this is what the author meant by his saying: he interpreted it as separation of bodies. And from that is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' (1) And Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, said: 'The female apostate is not killed.' (2) And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'The generality of the hadith is not abandoned by his statement and specification, and refraining from acting on it is like acting contrary to it; because refraining is forbidden, just like acting contrary to it.' And Allah knows best. (1) The hadith of Ibn Abbas: from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' – wording of Ibn Majah, and al-Bukhari and the rest of the authors of the Sunan also reported it in a story. (2) His statement: 'And Ibn Abbas said: The female apostate is not killed' – Ibn Abi Shaybah reported: 'Abd al-Rahim ibn Sulayman and Waki' narrated to us from Abu Hanifa from Asim from Abu Razin from Ibn Abbas who said: 'Women are not killed if they apostatize from Islam, but they are imprisoned and called to Islam, and they are compelled to it.' And al-Daraqutni reported it from the path of Abu Malik al-Nakha'i from Asim. I said: They have said: The place of this is when the marfu' is not general, and this marfu' is general, so how can it be sound? And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule about the principle that when a narrator (or a Companion) acts upon one of the possible meanings of a prophetic text, this does not constitute a rejection of the other possible meanings, nor does it prove that the narrator's interpretation is the only valid one. The author uses linguistic reasoning: the possibility (ihtimal) inherent in speech is not nullified by someone's interpretation (ta'wil).

The first example is the well-known hadith of Ibn Umar regarding the option of the sale session (khiyar al-majlis): 'The two parties to a sale have the option as long as they have not separated' (al-mutabayi'an bi'l-khiyar ma lam yatafarraqa). The word 'tafarruq' can mean both physical separation and separation by words (i.e., concluding the deal verbally). Ibn Umar interpreted it as physical separation, as evidenced by his practice of walking a bit after the sale to ensure finality. However, the author argues that this interpretation does not negate the other possibility (separation by words) because the word is a homonym (mushtarak) having two different meanings, and linguistic commonality is not invalidated by someone's interpretation.

The second example is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' (man baddala dinahu faqtuluhu). The apparent generality ('umum) of the hadith includes both male and female apostates. However, Ibn Abbas reported a ruling that the female apostate is not killed but imprisoned and compelled to return to Islam. The author uses this as another example of a narrator acting on one possible interpretation (that the general term 'whoever' is specified by context or other evidence, limiting it to males). But this does not invalidate the general meaning in other contexts.

The passage then records the Shafi'i objection: that one should not abandon the generality of the hadith based on the statement and specification of a single Companion, and refraining from acting on the general is equivalent to acting contrary to it, both being forbidden. The author does not give a full response but ends with 'And Allah knows best.' This indicates that the Hanafi position is that the Companion's interpretation is a valid specification (takhsis) even if the hadith is general, because the Companion's action is a form of bayan al-shar'i. The footnote (2) provides the chain for Ibn Abbas's statement, including a remark by the author questioning whether this applies when the marfu' hadith is general.

Key Terms
احتمال (ihtimal): Linguistic possibility — the capacity of a word or phrase to bear multiple meanings.
اشتراك (ishtirak): Homonymy — a single word having two or more different meanings (e.g., 'ayn for eye, spring, etc.).
تأويل (ta'wil): Interpretation — assigning one of the possible meanings to a word based on evidence or personal reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle stated in the passage, what is the legal effect of a narrator's acting on one possible meaning of a homonymous word in a prophetic hadith?
A) It establishes that meaning as the only correct one.
B) It does not invalidate the other possible meanings.
C) It automatically abrogates the hadith's generality.
D) It makes the narrator unreliable.

Key Takeaway
A narrator's interpretation of a general or ambiguous text does not reject other possible meanings; the text retains its full linguistic potential.
